The comb would pull my hair and there was always lots of hair in the comb. The newer versions smell, including &amp;#34;knock offs&amp;#34; or other brands.  I don&#x27;t think it is a problem specific to this vendor.  I looked on Wet Brush&#x27;s FaceBook page, and they did have some people complaining about the smell. Their response (paraphrasing here) was that because the rubber is so new, it can be difficult to know which ones may still have a stronger smell.  They suggested putting it outside in the sun for several hours to alleviate the smell.  I have tried this, but its turned cold here, and I have trees overhead in my back yard.  Next up I may try putting it under a heat lamp for a bit, etc.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I gave three stars because I do not think the odor is a problem from this vendor, but rather the Wet Brush itself, as there have been repeated problems, even when buying directly from department stores, etc.  I will continue to try new things (short of baking the brush!) to get rid of the smell.  Until then, I can&#x27;t use it.</li>

Since using it; some of the bristles on the brush became pushed down into the padding of brush. When used on my mothers hair which is very thin, curly and coarse due to health reasons. When I used this on my mothers hair (wet and dry); the product de-tangled very well but left a bit of frizz and some snagging of the hair along the way. The only downfall is that the WET brush doesn&#x27;t smooth the hair; it might create little to no frizz but that differs from the type and grade of hair YOU have. This brush is truly meant for de-tangling and NOT for styling purposes; i&#x27;d recommend a Denman 8 row brush for styling. Overall I give this product a 4/5 star rating for that the product needs a better, more sturdy manufacturing; other than that i&#x27;d recommend it to all members of a family; it does what it&#x27;s suppose to do.</li>

    <li> I have incredibly long hair and have always had an issue with it getting itself all wrapped up when I am sleeping. It often results in a giant clump on the back of my head, making it both difficult to reach and difficult to see. That has always made getting the tangles out quite a chore. I first noticed this product upon the &#x27;Related Items&#x27; section on Amazon while looking at detangling sprays and figured why not. More importantly, I was intrigued as to how this product could work, it looked just like any other paddle brush. Frankly, it sounded more like a gimmick than a legitimate product.  After using it for a few days, I think I know why.  The bristles are a bit longer, softer, and more flexible than that of most brushes. I suspect that is the key. When each bristle hits the tangle, it moves towards where the hair itself is headed versus forcing the hair to where the bristles are. This would result in moving the tangle down and slowly causing the clump to dissipate without tying it further into a knot like a regular brush or comb might. It might seem slow at first because of it, but the knot itself isn&#x27;t tightened and I think that&#x27;s more important than instant headway. Due to that key fact, the tangle in the end is easier to brush out, it has less kinks in it, and overall the process is much less painful.
